| `cellsAreOrbits_of_twin_cells` | 718-774 | `CellsAreOrbits` at **arbitrary** support whenever every same-cell pair is an order-undecided twin ‚ÄĒ the genuine-twin / module abelian regime (not CFI, which has no twins). The twin-reconstructible slice of the open localisation obligation. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `orbitRecoverableAt_of_twin_cells` | 776-795 | Oracle-vocabulary form of `cellsAreOrbits_of_twin_cells`: on the twin regime refinement computes the orbit partition at any node, with no depth bound. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `RecoverableByDepth` | 797-806 | Cascade-class membership for the oracle contract: there is a polynomially-bounded depth at which cells = orbits (the bound carries all the content). | Definition |
| `recoverableByDepth_cfi` | 816-822 | **(1a), proved for CFI** (axiom-free, odd-degree): recoverable by depth `cfi_depth_bound h` (‚Č§ baseSize ‚Č§ n/6). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `recoverableByDepth_scheme` | 824-836 | **(1a), proved for schemes** (axiom-free, rank 2 / `|J| = 1`): recoverable by depth 1, at the very node the oracle acts on. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `recoverableByDepth_pPolynomial` | 838-855 | **(1a), proved for the whole metric/DRG family** (axiom-free, P-polynomial / `|J|=1`): recoverable by depth 1, via `theorem_2_HOR_of_pPolynomial`. Generalizes `recoverableByDepth_scheme` (rank-2 only) to every P-polynomial schurian scheme graph ‚ÄĒ cycles, Johnson, Hamming, all DRGs ‚ÄĒ in one oracle-vocabulary export; depth-1 cells non-singleton (genuine recovery at the structural oracle's node). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `recoverableByDepth_univ` | 857-864 | Every graph is trivially recoverable by depth `n` (individualize everything), so only the *polynomial* depth bound is cascade-class content. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CascadeComplete` | 871-878 | Completeness contract: the oracle certifies every genuine `Aut_D`-orbit pair; with soundness it then computes the orbit relation exactly. | Definition |
| `certifies_iff_orbit` | 880-894 | For a sound and complete cascade oracle, it returns `some` exactly on the pairs sharing an `Aut_D`-orbit. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CellComplete` | 896-903 | The polynomial completeness contract: the oracle certifies every pair sharing a 1-WL cell (refinement-decidable). | Definition |
| `complete_of_cellComplete_recoverable` | 905-918 | **Key theorem.** At an orbit-recoverable node, certifying every same-cell pair already certifies every orbit ‚ÄĒ reducing orbit-completeness to a polynomial check. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `VerdictIsoInvariant` | 965-978 | Iso-invariance contract (strategy ¬ß15 gap 2): the oracle's verdict depends only on the iso-invariant 1-WL partition. Derivable ‚ÄĒ see `verdictIsoInvariant_of_complete`. | Definition |
| `cascadeComplete_of_localization` | 980-991 | Capstone: cell-completeness plus all-nodes recoverability yields `CascadeComplete`, naming the open localisation obligation as its hypotheses. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cascadeComplete_of_cellsAreOrbits` | 993-1004 | Capstone stated against the single open implication: cell-completeness plus `CellsAreOrbits` at every node yields `CascadeComplete`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `verdictIsoInvariant_of_complete` | 1006-1021 | **Key theorem.** A sound, complete oracle at orbit-recoverable nodes is automatically iso-invariant, so iso-invariance is part of localisation rather than a separate obligation. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `computes_orbits_of_complete` | 1023-1035 | Capstone: a sound and complete cascade oracle computes the `Aut_D`-orbit relation exactly (program-level correctness, given the completeness obligation). | ‚ÄĒ |

| `rankPerm_inv_mul_eq_of_match` | 1052-1064 | ¬ßC.4 M-B ‚ÄĒ the rank-composition identity behind `colourMatchPerm = g`: if `g` value-matches the two colourings (`Ōá‚āā ‚ąė g = Ōá‚āĀ`), then `(rankPerm Ōá‚āā)‚ĀĽ¬Ļ * rankPerm Ōá‚āĀ = g`. Pure `vertexRank_comp` reindexing, no graph structure. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `colourMatchPerm` | 1066-1076 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B ‚ÄĒ the colour-match permutation.** The explicit `Equiv.Perm` from the two *discrete* branch colourings, as the rank composition `(rankPerm Ōá_w)‚ĀĽ¬Ļ * (rankPerm Ōá_v)` (`Ōá_r = warmRefine adj P (indivWithRep n D r)`). Always well-defined given discreteness; `= g` at a recoverable node. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `colourMatchPerm_eq_of_orbit` | 1078-1091 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B completeness linchpin.** An `Aut_D` witness `g` (`g v = w`, `w ‚ąČ D`) value-matches the two branch colourings (`colourMatch_complete`), so `colourMatchPerm = g` ‚ÄĒ built from the colours, not assumed. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle` | 1092-1110 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B ‚ÄĒ the colour-match cascade oracle.** Constructs `colourMatchPerm` (when both footprints discrete) and returns it **iff** it verifies as an `Aut_D` orbit map (`IsAut ‚ąß P-preserving ‚ąß fixes D ‚ąß v ‚Ü¶ w`). Construct-and-check, not the existential shortcut. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `matchOracle_orbitMapSpec` | 1135-1145 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B soundness ‚ÄĒ `OrbitMapSpec`, unconditional.** When `matchOracle` fires, its four checks *are* the `OrbitPartition` witness conditions, so the returned perm certifies a genuine `Aut_D` orbit pair. No discreteness/recoverability hypothesis. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_cellComplete` | 1147-1183 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B completeness ‚ÄĒ `CellComplete`.** Conditional on every node one-step-discretizing (`hdisc`, = the exposure-depth witness / M-C / "B's core") and `CellsAreOrbits` everywhere (`hco`, = localisation): at a same-cell pair the orbit automorphism exists, `colourMatchPerm = g`, so the oracle fires. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_cascadeComplete` | 1185-1196 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B capstone ‚ÄĒ `CascadeComplete`.** `matchOracle` computes the orbit relation exactly, reduced to the two named-open hypotheses (discretizing depth + `CellsAreOrbits`); soundness is already unconditional. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_verdictIsoInvariant` | 1198-1212 | ¬ßC.4 **M-B ‚ÄĒ flag iso-invariance, free.** With soundness + completeness, `verdictIsoInvariant_of_complete` gives the verdict as a function of the iso-invariant 1-WL partition (strategy ¬ß15 gap 2) for `matchOracle` on the recoverable class. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `discrete_of_samePartition` | 1231-1234 | ¬ßC.4b Discreteness transfers across `samePartition`: `samePartition Ōá‚āĀ Ōá‚āā ‚Üí Discrete Ōá‚āĀ ‚Üí Discrete Ōá‚āā`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `warmRefine_samePartition` | 1236-1241 | ¬ßC.4b `warmRefine` respects `samePartition` (specialization of `warmRefine_agree_off'`, `D = ‚ąÖ`): equal-partition starts warm-refine to equal-partition results. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `samePartition_indivWithRep_insert` | 1243-1284 | ¬ßC.4b **Single-rep footprint = indexed `insert`.** For `r ‚ąČ D`, `indivWithRep n D r` and `individualizedColouring n (insert r D)` induce the same partition (`r` globally unique either way). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `discrete_indivWithRep_of_discrete_insert` | 1286-1295 | ¬ßC.4b **The M-B depth-witness bridge.** M-B's `hdisc` follows from discreteness of the *indexed* `individualizedColouring (insert r D)` ‚ÄĒ connecting the depth witness to the `RecoverableByDepth` framework, class-agnostically. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `indivWithSet` | 1312-1317 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C ‚ÄĒ multi-step uniform individualization.** Individualize the committed set `S` by index, plus an explored *set* `R` with a single uniform fresh colour `n+1`. Generalizes `indivWithRep` (`R = {r}`); uniform on `R` is forced by transport (an orbit aut moves `R`). | Definition |
| `indivWithRep_eq_indivWithSet` | 1319-1322 | ¬ßC.5 `indivWithRep n S r = indivWithSet n S {r}` ‚ÄĒ the singleton bridge to M-B. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `indivWithSet_transport` | 1324-1343 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C transport.** An orbit aut `g` fixing `S` with `R‚āā = R‚āĀ.image g` carries the branch-`R‚āĀ` colouring onto branch-`R‚āā` (`Ōá‚āā ‚ąė g = Ōá‚āĀ`); the `indivWithRep_transport` generalization (uniform colour on the moved set is what makes it hold). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `IsColourMatchSet` | 1345-1349 | ¬ßC.5 The multi-step colour-match relation: `t` matches branch-`R‚āā`'s refined colours to branch-`R‚āĀ`'s. The `IsColourMatch` generalization. | Definition |
| `colourMatchSet_complete` | 1351-1358 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C completeness brick.** The orbit aut `g` (fixing `S`, `R‚āā = R‚āĀ.image g`) *is* a colour-match (`warmRefine_transport ‚ąė indivWithSet_transport`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `colourMatchSet_unique` | 1360-1370 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C uniqueness brick.** At a discrete branch-`R‚āā` footprint any colour-match `= g`, via the colouring-generic `colourMatch_eq_aut`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `harvestSet_isAut_of_discrete` | 1372-1382 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C harvest brick.** At a discrete branch-`R‚āā` footprint the colour-match candidate verifies (`= g`) ‚ÄĒ the harvest now fires at a footprint discretized by an explored *set* (a sequence), not just one rep. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `colourMatchPermSet` | 1384-1391 | ¬ßC.5 **M-C ‚ÄĒ the multi-step colour-match permutation.** The rank composition `(rankPerm Ōá_{R‚āā})‚ĀĽ¬Ļ * (rankPerm Ōá_{R‚āĀ})` for set footprints; `colourMatchPerm` is the `R‚āĀ={v}, R‚āā={w}` case. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `colourMatchPermSet_eq_of_orbit` | 1393-1403 | ¬ßC.5 `colourMatchPermSet = g` at a recoverable set-footprint (`rankPerm_inv_mul_eq_of_match` ‚Üź `vertexRank_comp` + `colourMatchSet_complete`); the multi-step `colourMatchPerm_eq_of_orbit`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `colourMatchSet_exists_of_cellsAreOrbits` | 1405-1418 | ¬ßC.5 **The multi-step firing certificate exists.** From `CellsAreOrbits` at a same-cell pair, for *any* exploration set `R‚āĀ` the orbit aut `g`, partner `R‚āā = R‚āĀ.image g`, and the colour-match all exist. The open piece (M-D) is that the oracle's branch-`w` set *is* `R‚āĀ.image g` (lockstep). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSet` | 1431-1451 | ¬ßC.6 **M-D ‚ÄĒ the multi-step colour-match oracle.** Like `matchOracle` but individualizes a whole explored *set* `expand chain r` (per an exploration selector) on top of the committed path; constructs `colourMatchPermSet`, returns it **iff** it verifies `IsAut ‚ąß P-preserving ‚ąß fixes D ‚ąß v ‚Ü¶ w`. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `matchOracleSet_orbitMapSpec` | 1480-1490 | ¬ßC.6 **M-D soundness ‚ÄĒ `OrbitMapSpec`, unconditional.** When it fires the four checks *are* the `OrbitPartition` witness; no discreteness/recoverability/lockstep hypothesis. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `LockstepExpand` | 1492-1502 | ¬ßC.6 **The lockstep correspondence** as equivariance of the exploration rule: any `P`-preserving automorphism fixing the committed path carries one branch's exploration set onto the other's (`expand chain (g v) = (expand chain v).image g`). Discharged for `forcedExpand` (`Cascade.lean`). | Definition |
| `matchOracleSet_cellComplete` | 1504-1544 | ¬ßC.6 **M-D completeness ‚ÄĒ `CellComplete`.** Reduced to set-footprint discreteness (the multi-step depth witness) + `CellsAreOrbits` + `LockstepExpand`: the lockstep supplies `R‚āā = R‚āĀ.image g`, so `colourMatchPermSet = g` and the oracle fires. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSet_cascadeComplete` | 1546-1558 | ¬ßC.6 **M-D capstone ‚ÄĒ `CascadeComplete`** (the multi-step oracle computes the orbit relation exactly), reduced to the three named-open hypotheses. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSet_verdictIsoInvariant` | 1560-1573 | ¬ßC.6 **M-D ‚ÄĒ flag iso-invariance, free** (via `verdictIsoInvariant_of_complete`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_fires_of_insertDiscrete` | 1606-1629 | ¬ßC.7 **Honest per-node firing (`hco`-free).** At a node where committing the path plus the query rep discretizes (the indexed `RecoverableByDepth` form, bridged by ¬ßC.4b), `matchOracle` fires on **any** genuine `Aut_D` orbit pair `(v,w)` (`v,w ‚ąČ D`) ‚ÄĒ the orbit witness is consumed directly, so no `CellsAreOrbits`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_orbit_of_fire_mono` | 1631-1645 | ¬ßC.7 **Propagate via `mono`.** A merge certified at a node holds at every shallower committed set `S ‚äÜ chain.D` (`OrbitPartition.mono`) ‚ÄĒ the "fire deep, prune shallow" step. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracle_certifies_iff_orbit_of_insertDiscrete` | 1647-1673 | ¬ßC.7 **Exact orbit decider at the discretizing depth.** At a footprint-discretizing node, `matchOracle` fires on `(v,w)` **iff** they are a genuine `Aut_D` orbit pair (`hco`-free). Limits: holds only under the discreteness hypotheses (cascade depth), and decides the *path-fixing* `Aut_D`, not global `Aut`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `indivWithSeq` | 1694-1699 | ¬ßC.8 **Level-coloured exploration sequence (Leg 1).** Committed `S` by index plus the `i`-th element of `rs` by its *position* colour `n+1+i`; the position colouring (not vertex index) is what transports under an orbit automorphism. | Definition |
| `samePartition_indivWithSeq` | 1710-1778 | ¬ßC.8 **A1: level-coloured sequence = indexed union.** `indivWithSeq n S rs` and the indexed `individualizedColouring n (S ‚ą™ rs.toFinset)` induce the same partition (each `rs`-vertex globally unique); unconditional. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `discrete_indivWithSeq_of_discrete_union` | 1780-1791 | ¬ßC.8 **The Leg-1 depth-witness bridge (sequence).** Sequence-footprint discreteness follows from discreteness of the indexed `individualizedColouring n (S ‚ą™ rs.toFinset)`, so `hdiscSeq ‚üł recoverableByDepth`. Sequence generalization of `discrete_indivWithRep_of_discrete_insert`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `idxOf_map_of_injective` | 1805-1817 | ¬ßC.8 **Position preserved by `map`.** `(l.map g).idxOf (g a) = l.idxOf a` for a permutation `g` ‚ÄĒ the pure-list core of sequence transport. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `indivWithSeq_transport` | 1819-1840 | ¬ßC.8 **A2 transport.** An orbit aut `g` fixing `S` with `rs‚āā = rs‚āĀ.map g` carries the branch-`rs‚āĀ` level colouring onto branch-`rs‚āā` (`Ōá‚āā ‚ąė g = Ōá‚āĀ`) ‚ÄĒ position via `idxOf_map_of_injective`, off-sequence via `individualizedColouring` invariance. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `IsColourMatchSeq` | 1842-1845 | ¬ßC.8 The sequence colour-match relation (`IsColourMatchSet` analogue): `t` matches branch-`rs‚āā`'s refined colours to branch-`rs‚āĀ`'s. | Definition |
| `colourMatchSeq_complete` | 1847-1854 | ¬ßC.8 **Sequence completeness brick.** The orbit aut `g` (fixing `S`, `rs‚āā = rs‚āĀ.map g`) *is* a colour-match (`warmRefine_transport ‚ąė indivWithSeq_transport`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `colourMatchPermSeq` | 1856-1863 | ¬ßC.8 **The sequence colour-match permutation.** Rank composition `(rankPerm Ōá_{rs‚āā})‚ĀĽ¬Ļ * rankPerm Ōá_{rs‚āĀ}` for level-coloured footprints; `colourMatchPermSet` with the uniform set replaced by the sequence. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `colourMatchSeq_exists_of_cellsAreOrbits` | 1877-1890 | ¬ßC.8 **The level-coloured firing certificate exists.** From `CellsAreOrbits`, for any sequence `rs‚āĀ` the orbit aut `g`, partner `rs‚āā = rs‚āĀ.map g`, and the colour-match exist. The open piece is the ordered lockstep (A2b). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSeq` | 1903-1923 | ¬ßC.8 **The multi-step sequence colour-match oracle.** Like `matchOracleSet` but individualizes the ordered sequence `expand chain r` via `indivWithSeq` (so its depth witness is A1-reducible); construct-and-check on `colourMatchPermSeq`. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `matchOracleSeq_orbitMapSpec` | 1951-1960 | ¬ßC.8 **Sequence soundness ‚ÄĒ `OrbitMapSpec`, unconditional.** When it fires the four checks *are* the `OrbitPartition` witness. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `LockstepExpandSeq` | 1962-1973 | ¬ßC.8 **The sequence lockstep.** The ordered (`map`, not `image`) `LockstepExpand` analogue: `expand chain (g v) = (expand chain v).map g`. Strictly stronger than the set lockstep; provably false in the multi-step regime (`lockstep_disc_imp_stab_trivial`). | Definition |
| `matchOracleSeq_cellComplete` | 1975-2014 | ¬ßC.8 **Sequence completeness ‚ÄĒ `CellComplete`.** Reduced to `hdiscSeq` (A1-reducible) + `hco` + `LockstepExpandSeq`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSeq_cascadeComplete` | 2016-2028 | ¬ßC.8 **Sequence capstone ‚ÄĒ `CascadeComplete`**, reduced to the same three hypotheses (the last jointly unsatisfiable with `hdiscSeq` for multi-step ‚ÄĒ see `lockstep_disc_imp_stab_trivial`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `matchOracleSeq_verdictIsoInvariant` | 2030-2043 | ¬ßC.8 **Sequence flag iso-invariance, free** (via `verdictIsoInvariant_of_complete`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `lockstep_disc_imp_stab_trivial` | 2075-2109 | ¬ßC.8 **The discretizing-oracle limit (conservation of obstruction).** `LockstepExpandSeq ‚ąß hdiscSeq ‚üĻ stab_{Aut_D}(v) = 1`: the sequence oracle's completeness hypotheses hold jointly only in the single-rep regime, so the discretizing colour-match cannot harvest a multi-step moved orbit (‚Üí cross-branch / Schreier‚ÄďSims). | ‚ÄĒ |
## ChainDescent/LinearOracle.lean

The linear-oracle / abelian-stripping work (tractable-buildout B2; plan + status in `docs/chain-descent-linear-oracle.md` ¬ß8.2). Built on the ¬ß15.8 scaffolding (`DirAssignment`/`flipPair`/`LinearOracleSpec`/`LeafTwistSpec`/`canonAdj`). Builds axiom-clean (`refineStep`/`refineStep_iff` + foundationals), no `sorry`. **B2 soundness core DONE 2026-05-30:** ¬ßL.1 soundness anchor, ¬ßL.2 the *forced* candidate twist (rank rebasing ‚ÄĒ the construction is determined, not searched; the `canonAdj_rebase` bridge), ¬ßL.3 abelian `Z‚āā^d` structure. Remaining: `canonForm` lex-min tie (needs descent-with-pruning model), completeness, lifting twists to subgroup `N` (Part A).

### ¬ßL.1 ‚ÄĒ Soundness anchor (B2.1)

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `RealizesFlip` | 52-61 | **Soundness anchor.** The relation "twist `t` relabels branch `ŌÉ`'s leaf to the flipped branch `flipPair ŌÉ a b`'s leaf" ‚ÄĒ the `LeafTwistSpec` conclusion with the partner branch pinned to the flip, i.e. the pruning justification. | Definition |
| `TwistWitness` | 63-83 | The verified data a twist discovery returns: the decided pair `(a,b)`, the candidate permutation `t`, its `IsAut` proof (the ¬ß4.5 edge-check, sole soundness anchor), and a `RealizesFlip` proof. | Structure |
| `twistOracle` | 85-95 | A concrete `LinearOracleSpec` parameterised by an abstracted `discover` function (C#-side canonical-id matching); returns the verified automorphism from a `TwistWitness`, `none` otherwise. Verification lives inside the witness, so every output is a genuine automorphism. | Definition |
| `twistOracle_leafTwist` | 97-116 | **Key theorem (B2.1 discharge).** `twistOracle` satisfies `LeafTwistSpec`, with the flipped branch as the explicit witness `ŌÉ' = flipPair ŌÉ` (sharper than the bare existential) ‚ÄĒ closing the pruning-justification contract for any sound discovery. | ‚ÄĒ |

### ¬ßL.2 ‚ÄĒ The forced candidate twist (B2.2 + most of B2.3)

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `canonAdj_rebase` | 159-174 | **The rebasing bridge.** Relabelling `ŌÉ`'s canonical leaf by the rank rebasing `rankPerm ŌÄ_{ŌÉ'} * (rankPerm ŌÄ_ŌÉ)‚ĀĽ¬Ļ` yields `ŌÉ'`'s leaf; the flip is the `ŌÉ' = flipPair ŌÉ` instance. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `candidateTwist` | 184-192 | **The forced candidate twist** for decision `(a,b)`: the rank rebasing `rankPerm ŌÄ_flip * (rankPerm ŌÄ_ŌÉ)‚ĀĽ¬Ļ`. Always realises the flip; the twist is determined, not searched. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `candidateTwist_realizesFlip` | 194-201 | The forced candidate always realises the flip ‚ÄĒ the construction is forced, with no ambiguity. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `candidateTwist_unique` | 203-215 | **Determinacy.** The candidate is the unique permutation rank-aligning `ŌÉ` to the flipped branch ‚ÄĒ the leaf-level iso-invariance gate, making twist discovery deterministic in iso-invariant rank data. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `twistWitness_of_isAut` | 217-234 | The oracle reduces to one check: a verified-automorphism forced candidate yields a complete `TwistWitness`. Discovery is a single decidable edge-check. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `canonicalTwistOracle` | 235-249 | **The canonical twist oracle.** A fully concrete `LinearOracleSpec`: for the selected pair, compute the forced candidate and return it iff it verifies as an automorphism. The only abstracted piece is pair selection (soundness-irrelevant). | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `canonicalTwistOracle_leafTwist` | 251-259 | **Key theorem.** `canonicalTwistOracle` satisfies `LeafTwistSpec` (it is a `twistOracle`) ‚ÄĒ a concrete verified linear oracle, sound by construction. | ‚ÄĒ |

### ¬ßL.3 ‚ÄĒ Abelian structure (B2.4, partial)

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `candidateTwist_flip_inv` | 282-291 | **`Z‚āā` involution.** The forced candidate for the flip-back is the inverse of the candidate for the flip; with `flipPair_comm` this is the elementary-abelian `Z‚āā^d` structure of the residual. | ‚ÄĒ |

### ¬ßL.4 ‚ÄĒ Completeness / effectiveness (when the oracle fires)

Characterizes *when* the oracle fires and proves firing is semantically justified. The
oracle is complete exactly on the **abelian regime** (forced candidate ‚ąą Aut) ‚ÄĒ the
calculator ¬ß6 boundary; the general converse fails (conjugation gap). The
abelian-sufficiency lemma (forced candidate IsAut for genuine abelian flips, via
`warm_6_2` rank machinery) is the open core scoped in the ¬ßL.4 doc-comment.

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `isAut_candidateTwist_iff_aligned` | 329-344 | **Firing characterisation.** The forced candidate is an automorphism iff some automorphism is rank-aligned (`g ¬∑ ŌÄ_ŌÉ = ŌÄ_flip`) ‚ÄĒ so the whole completeness question is "does a rank-aligned automorphism exist?" | ‚ÄĒ |
| `RealizableFlip` | 346-352 | The decision is a genuine `Aut(adj)` symmetry: some automorphism realises the flip (the two branches are isomorphic) ‚ÄĒ what pruning should require. | Definition |
| `realizableFlip_of_isAut_candidateTwist` | 354-365 | **Firing is semantically justified.** When the forced candidate verifies, the branches are genuinely `Aut(adj)`-equivalent (the candidate is the witness) ‚ÄĒ pruning reflects a real symmetry. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `canonicalTwistOracle_isSome_iff` | 367-383 | **Key theorem.** Given the pair selector returns `(a,b)`, the oracle fires iff the forced candidate is an automorphism ‚ÄĒ the entire completeness question is one decidable edge-check. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `candidateTwist_flipBack_isAut` | 385-396 | **`Z‚āā`-direction consistency.** If the forced candidate for `ŌÉ ‚Üí flip` verifies, so does the candidate for the flip-back ‚ÄĒ the oracle prunes both directions of a genuine `Z‚āā` decision consistently. | ‚ÄĒ |

### ¬ßL.5 ‚ÄĒ Toward abelian sufficiency (partial)

The open core of completeness ‚ÄĒ *forced candidate ‚ąą Aut for abelian decisions* ‚ÄĒ needs
gadget-level rank-alignment (at a leaf both branches are discrete, so `warm_6_2`'s
partition equality is vacuous; the content is in the rank order). Provable progress:

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `candidateTwist_eq_one_of_rankPerm_eq` | 424-435 | **Absorbed decision.** Equal leaf rank permutations force the candidate to be the identity ‚ÄĒ the degenerate end of the abelian regime. | ‚ÄĒ |

### ¬ßL.7 ‚ÄĒ The CFI bridge (M1b): candidate as a conjugate of a graph automorphism

Now that `refineStep` is concrete, the cross-config transport (`¬ß16.2b` in ChainDescent.lean)
lets us express the forced candidate via a *real* automorphism. A **config-swap** `g` carries the
ŌÉ-branch config onto the flip-branch config; it forces `ŌÄ_ŌÉ = ŌÄ_flip ¬∑ g`, so the candidate is the
`ŌÄ_ŌÉ`-conjugate of `g‚ĀĽ¬Ļ`. This reduces the opaque `IsAut candidate adj` to the structural gadget
rank-alignment, isolating the genuine CFI nut (shared with Tier-3a B1 `hwit`): (1) a config-swap
exists, (2) its `ŌÄ_ŌÉ`-conjugate is an automorphism.

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `ConfigSwap` | 587-599 | A config-swap for decision `(a,b)`: a graph automorphism carrying the ŌÉ-branch configuration onto the flip-branch configuration (fixes `ŌáőĻ`, sends `ŌÉ.ŌÉ` to `(flipPair ŌÉ).ŌÉ`). For CFI, the gadget twist swapping the decided pair. | Structure |
| `configSwap_rankPerm` / `_flip` | The leaf rank perms differ by `g`: `ŌÄ_ŌÉ = ŌÄ_flip ¬∑ g` (resp. `ŌÄ_flip = ŌÄ_ŌÉ ¬∑ g‚ĀĽ¬Ļ`), from transport + `vertexRank_comp`. | axiom-light |
| `candidateTwist_eq_conjugate` | 627-637 | **The rank-space reduction.** Given a config-swap `g`, the forced candidate is the `ŌÄ_ŌÉ`-conjugate of `g‚ĀĽ¬Ļ` (`candidateTwist = ŌÄ_ŌÉ ¬∑ g‚ĀĽ¬Ļ ¬∑ ŌÄ_ŌÉ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ`) ‚ÄĒ the opaque rebasing exposed as a conjugate of a genuine automorphism. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `isAut_candidateTwist_iff_conjugate` | 639-650 | **The reduction.** `IsAut candidate adj ‚ÜĒ IsAut (ŌÄ_ŌÉ ¬∑ g‚ĀĽ¬Ļ ¬∑ ŌÄ_ŌÉ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ) adj` ‚ÄĒ the rank-space firing obligation is exactly the gadget rank-alignment, the concrete nut shared with Tier-3a B1. | ‚ÄĒ |

**¬ßL.7b ‚ÄĒ vertex-model soundness (Approach C, the faithful C# model).** A config-swap is a real
graph automorphism, so both branches give the *same canonical leaf* ‚ÄĒ no rank-alignment needed. This
is the soundness the C# `TwistConstruction` actually uses (it verifies a vertex automorphism, not the
rank rebasing).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `canonAdj_eq_of_configSwap` | 661-676 | **Equal canonical leaves.** A config-swap implies both branches produce the identical canonical leaf ‚ÄĒ the vertex-model soundness statement (pruning the flip branch loses nothing), needing no rank-alignment. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `realizableFlip_of_configSwap` | 678-692 | A config-swap implies `RealizableFlip` (identity witness, since the leaves coincide) ‚ÄĒ the decision is a genuine `Aut(adj)` symmetry with no rank-alignment obligation. | ‚ÄĒ |

**¬ßL.8 ‚ÄĒ CFI completeness: config-swap from a swapping automorphism (M1c step 3, the cascade-1b bridge).**
*Where a config-swap comes from.* A swapping automorphism `g` (`g a = b`, `g b = a`) is exactly an
`OrbitPartition adj P S a b` witness specialised to the size-2 decision cell ‚ÄĒ the cascade oracle's
currency. So linear-oracle CFI completeness reduces to the **shared cascade-1b** obligation
(bounded-depth half `recoverableByDepth_cfi` proved; decision-node-depth bridge open, *not* `GI‚ąąP`).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `configSwap_of_aut` | 724-767 | **General constructor (the `hwit` entry point).** *Any* swapping automorphism `g` (`g a = b`, `g b = a`) that fixes `ŌáőĻ` and preserves `ŌÉ.ŌÉ` *off the flip pair* (`ŌÉ.ŌÉ (g v)(g u) = ŌÉ.ŌÉ v u` for `(v,u) ‚ąČ {(a,b),(b,a)}`) is a `ConfigSwap` ‚ÄĒ `g` need **not** be a transposition (may move the whole coupled component). Removes the config-swap *packaging* from the open content: once the CFI gadget twist `g` and its off-pair `ŌÉ`-action are known, the `ConfigSwap` is built with no rank-alignment. | Definition |
| `configSwap_of_swap` | 769-820 | **Closed instance (the `Z‚āā` twin-swap).** A ŌÉ-cell-coherent transposition automorphism (`g` swaps `a,b`, fixes the rest and `ŌáőĻ`) is a `ConfigSwap` ‚ÄĒ the simplest genuine abelian decision. Now a thin specialisation of `configSwap_of_aut` (transposition ‚áí off-pair preservation = ŌÉ-cell-coherence). | Definition |
| `configSwap_of_twin` | 822-850 | **The twin ‚Üí config-swap bridge.** An (adj, ŌÉ)-twin decision pair (adjacency-twin on a simple graph plus ŌÉ-cell-coherent, `ŌáőĻ a = ŌáőĻ b`) admits a `ConfigSwap` via the transposition `(a b)` ‚ÄĒ the linear-oracle analog of `cellsAreOrbits_of_twin_cells`, both oracles firing on the same twin/module class through one shared lemma. Not CFI (which has no twins). | Definition |
| `ConfigSwapRecoverable` | 852-862 | **Decision-node recoverability** (the named cascade-1b obligation for the linear oracle): every leaf decision admits a config-swap. The graph-level analog of `AbelianSufficiencyHolds`; open discharge `configSwapRecoverable_of_cfi` is downstream. | Definition |
| `canonAdj_eq_of_configSwapRecoverable` | 864-875 | **Capstone (pruning soundness).** Config-swap-recoverability implies both branches give the identical canonical leaf at every decision ‚ÄĒ reducing the oracle's effectiveness to the single `ConfigSwapRecoverable` hypothesis. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `realizableFlip_of_configSwapRecoverable` | 877-888 | **Capstone (real symmetry).** Config-swap-recoverability implies every leaf decision is a genuine `Aut(adj)` symmetry ‚ÄĒ vertex-model completeness, no rank-alignment needed. | ‚ÄĒ |

**¬ßL.9 ‚ÄĒ CFI gadget twist fires the oracle (Phase 6a: wiring the Stage-3 cycle-space flip).** The
Stage-3 gadget flip (`CFI.lean ¬ß15`, `IsCFI'.cfiFlipAut`) is now constructed; this section wires it into
`configSwap_of_aut` and reduces `ConfigSwapRecoverable` for CFI to the existence of the right cycle `F`
per decision.

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `configSwap_of_cfiFlipAut` | **The CFI gadget twist is a config-swap** (unconditional bridge). `configSwap_of_aut` instantiated with `g := cfiFlipAut F` (an `Aut(adj)` involution by `isAut_cfiFlipAut`): if the flip swaps `(a,b)`, fixes `ŌáőĻ`, and carries `ŌÉ` off the pair, it is a `ConfigSwap`. The concrete soundness ‚ÄĒ the vertex-space gadget twist (the C#'s witness) fires the oracle, no rank-alignment. | Definition |
| `CFIGadgetFlippable` | **The named cascade-1b residual.** Every leaf decision admits an even-symmetric cycle `F` whose gadget flip swaps `(a,b)`, fixes `ŌáőĻ`, carries `ŌÉ` off the pair. Commits the CFI witness to the gadget-flip mechanism (matching the C#); the open content is purely `F`'s existence per decision (cascade-1b). | Definition |
| `configSwapRecoverable_of_cfi` | **`ConfigSwapRecoverable` for CFI via the gadget flip.** `CFIGadgetFlippable h ‚Üí ConfigSwapRecoverable` ‚ÄĒ the discharge reduced to its irreducible combinatorial core (the decision-local even cycle's existence). Feeds the capstones ‚üĻ oracle fires on every CFI decision. | ‚ÄĒ |

Open (not a `sorry`): **`CFIGadgetFlippable`** ‚ÄĒ that the decision-local even cycle `F` *exists* for every
decision (the flip is built and proven sound; what remains is the cycle through the decision edge, local
to the decided gadget). Its three per-decision obligations (swap `(a,b)`, fix `ŌáőĻ`, carry `ŌÉ` off the
pair) are the descent-coherence content of cascade-1b ‚ÄĒ the decision-node-depth half, shared with the
cascade oracle, *not* `GI‚ąąP`.

**¬ßL.9 follow-on ‚ÄĒ the conditions reduced to locality + cell-coherence.** Decouples the gadget-flip
mechanics from the descent's cell structure, so the residual is the cascade-1b shape (F-locality +
cell-coherence), not the opaque `configSwap_of_aut` package.

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `swapsConfig_off_pair_of_local` | **The ŌÉ-off-pair reduction (general `g`, reusable).** Any `g` swapping `(a,b)`, fixing decided vertices off `{a,b}`, preserving the decided set and `P‚āÄ`, satisfies the off-pair condition given only **ŌÉ-cell-coherence** at `(a,b)`. Off-D via `agrees_off` + P‚āÄ-invariance; on-D via the coherence case-analysis. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `preserves_D_of_involutive_local` | Decided-set preservation for an involutive local swap (`g x ‚ąą D ‚ÜĒ x ‚ąą D` from `g¬≤=id` + swap + fix-off-`{a,b}`). The `hgD` input above, discharged for the gadget flip. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cfiFlipAut_fixesŌáőĻ_of_support` | **The `hgŌá` reduction.** The flip fixes `ŌáőĻ` once it does on the F-touched gadgets ‚ÄĒ Phase-4 locality fixes every `F`-free gadget outright. Reduces global `hgŌá` to ŌáőĻ-coherence on the (small) F-support. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `configSwap_of_cfiFlipAut_local` | **The reduced bridge.** A `ConfigSwap` from {`F` even+symmetric, swap, **F is D-local**, ŌÉ-cell-coherent, `P‚āÄ` Aut-invariant, ŌáőĻ-coherent on F-support} ‚ÄĒ the three `configSwap_of_aut` conditions discharged via the reductions above. | Definition |
| `CFIGadgetFlippableLocal` | The reduced per-decision predicate: an even-symmetric **D-local** `F` whose flip swaps `(a,b)`, with ŌÉ cell-coherent and ŌáőĻ coherent on the F-support. The conditions are now the descent-coherence / cycle-locality (cascade-1b) facts. | Definition |
| `configSwapRecoverable_of_cfi_local` | `ConfigSwapRecoverable` from `CFIGadgetFlippableLocal` (+ `P‚āÄ` Aut-invariance) ‚ÄĒ the discharge via the decoupled hypotheses. | ‚ÄĒ |

**¬ßL.9 (C1b.1) ‚ÄĒ the CFI glue: parity-pair decisions.** Reduces `CFIGadgetFlippableLocal` to the
explicit-edge form, discharging the swap obligation in advance (via C1b.0).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `CFIParityDecisionFlippable` | The reduced cascade-1b hypothesis: every decision `(a,b)` is the parity-pair of a base edge `{v,w}` (`a = e^{b‚āÄ}_{v‚Üíw}`, `b = e^{¬¨b‚āÄ}`) admitting an even-symmetric cycle `F` with `{v,w} ‚ąą F`, D-local, ŌÉ/ŌáőĻ cell-coherent. The swap is no longer an obligation (it's `cfiFlipAut_swaps_endpointVertex`); only cycle existence + coherence remain. | Definition |
| `cfiGadgetFlippableLocal_of_parity` | **The C1b.1 glue.** `CFIParityDecisionFlippable ‚Üí CFIGadgetFlippableLocal` ‚ÄĒ the body's two swap conjuncts from `cfiFlipAut_endpointVertex` + `F v w = true`; the rest passes through. Open content narrows to C1b.2 (cycle exists) + C1b.3 (decisions are parity-pairs + coherence). | ‚ÄĒ |

Transport chain it builds on (ChainDescent.lean `¬ß16.2b`): `signature_transport`, `sigKey_transport`,
`refineStep_transport`, `iterate_refineStep_transport`, `warmRefine_transport` ‚ÄĒ cross-config (two
`(P,Ōá)` related by an automorphism), the value-level generalisation of the `*_invariant_of_isAut`
chain, newly provable because `refineStep` is concrete. All axiom-light.

### ¬ßL.6 ‚ÄĒ Relativized completeness (the retargeting)

The general completeness statement ("forced candidate fires whenever the branches are
isomorphic") *provably* cannot close ‚ÄĒ a realizing aut agrees with the forced candidate only
up to a conjugate of `Aut(adj)` (`rankPerm_comp`), the split-or-Johnson wall *by design*, and
the **same gap the a-priori cascade oracle carries** (`CascadeOracle.lean` ¬ß4.3). The fix is
the cascade oracle's **Phase-B move**: relativize completeness to the recoverable/abelian
class and reduce it to orbit recovery. This scaffold names the relativized target and isolates
the one open obligation (`AbelianSufficiencyHolds` on the CFI class ‚ÄĒ the leaf-level instance
of orbit recovery, the same nut as Tier-3a B1's `hwit`).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `RankAligned` | 482-490 | The algebraic firing condition: a rank-aligned automorphism exists (`‚ąÉ g ‚ąą Aut(adj), g ¬∑ ŌÄ_ŌÉ = ŌÄ_flip`). The oracle fires exactly when this holds. | Definition |
| `isAut_candidateTwist_iff_rankAligned` | 492-500 | **Interface.** The forced candidate is an automorphism iff `RankAligned` ‚ÄĒ the completeness question restated against the named predicate. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `AbelianSufficiency` | 502-512 | **The per-decision relativized completeness target.** `RealizableFlip ‚Üí IsAut candidate`: if the flip is a real symmetry then the forced candidate verifies. False in the non-abelian regime (the wall); the claim to discharge on the abelian/cascade class. | Definition |
| `oracleFires_of_abelianSufficiency` | 514-529 | **Capstone (what suffices).** `AbelianSufficiency` plus a real symmetry implies the oracle fires ‚ÄĒ the linear-oracle analog of cascade's `cascadeComplete_of_localization`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `abelianSufficiency_of_rankPerm_eq` | 531-542 | **Non-vacuous closed instance.** The absorbed decision is abelian-sufficient (candidate `= 1 ‚ąą Aut` outright) ‚ÄĒ validates the scaffold against a real instance. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `AbelianSufficiencyHolds` | 544-552 | The graph-level discharge target: every leaf decision is abelian-sufficient. Open obligation `abelianSufficiencyHolds_of_cfi` is downstream (via `theorem_1_HOR_cfi_oddDeg`, the same nut as Tier-3a B1's `hwit`). | Definition |
| `oracleFires_of_abelianSufficiencyHolds` | 554-568 | **Graph-level capstone.** `AbelianSufficiencyHolds` implies the oracle fires at every leaf decision that is a real symmetry ‚ÄĒ relativized completeness on the abelian class. | ‚ÄĒ |

## ChainDescent/Group.lean

Part A (A1‚ÄďA3) of `docs/chain-descent-tier3-tractable-buildout.md` ‚ÄĒ the group object
the orbit-recovery program deliberately avoided, now needed for Tier-3 vocabulary
(`H‚āÄ ‚äĶ ‚Ä¶ ‚äĶ H_k`, quotient graphs). Pure glue over Mathlib group theory + the existing
`IsAut` lemmas; **no `refineStep`** dependency (axioms `[propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound]`).
A4 (the quotient *graph* `G/H` + cell = quotient-vertex lemma) is **not** here ‚ÄĒ it is the
medium-risk Mathlib gap gating B1.

### A1 ‚ÄĒ `Aut(G)` as a group

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `AutGroup adj` | ¬ßA1 **The automorphism group.** `{ŌÄ | IsAut ŌÄ adj}` as a `Subgroup (Equiv.Perm (Fin n))` ‚ÄĒ the group object Tier-3 vocabulary (`H‚āÄ ‚äĶ ‚Ä¶ ‚äĶ H_k`, quotient graphs) is stated over. | Definition |
| `mem_autGroup` | 69-70 | Membership in `AutGroup adj` is exactly `IsAut ŌÄ adj` (`@[simp]` unfolding). | `@[simp]` |
| `orbitPartition_iff_autGroup` | 72-87 | ¬ßA1 **The `OrbitPartition` ‚ÜĒ `AutGroup` bridge.** Repackages the bare permutation of the orbit relation as a genuine group element in the pointwise-`S`-stabilizer that preserves `P`, keeping `OrbitPartition` the working object while exposing the group element where the chain needs it. | ‚ÄĒ |

### A2 ‚ÄĒ Action on vertices + orbit bridge

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `autGroup_smul` | 96-98 | ¬ßA2 The subgroup action's `smul` is permutation application: `g ‚ÄĘ v = (‚ÜĎg) v` (`@[simp]`). | `@[simp]` |
| `mem_orbit_autGroup_iff` | 100-109 | ¬ßA2 **Orbit membership, unfolded.** `w` lies in `v`'s `AutGroup`-orbit iff some automorphism sends `v` to `w` (the pure-orbit form, before `OrbitPartition`'s `P`-preservation refinement). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `mem_orbit_autGroup_iff_orbitPartition` | 111-125 | ¬ßA2 **The orbit bridge.** Under `P`-invariance, `v`'s `AutGroup`-orbit coincides with the root relation `OrbitPartition adj P ‚ąÖ` ‚ÄĒ the group-level reading of the support backbone's root case. | ‚ÄĒ |

### A3 ‚ÄĒ Normal subgroup chains

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `LayerChain adj` | ¬ßA3 A finite descending chain `AutGroup adj = layer 0 ‚äĶ ‚Ä¶ ‚äĶ layer len = ‚ä•`, each layer relatively normal in its predecessor ‚ÄĒ the `H‚āÄ ‚äĶ ‚Ä¶ ‚äĶ H_k` substrate Tier-3a (B1) reasons over. | Structure |
| `LayerChain.trivial` | ¬ßA3 **The trivial chain** `AutGroup adj ‚äĶ ‚ä•` (length 1); witnesses `LayerChain` is inhabited. | Definition |

### A4 ‚ÄĒ quotient graph + cell = quotient-vertex

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `orbitSetoid adj P S` | ¬ßA4 The `Aut_S`-orbit relation `OrbitPartition adj P S` packaged as a `Setoid` from its proved `refl`/`symm`/`trans`. | Definition |
| `OrbitQuotient adj P S` | ¬ßA4 **The quotient vertex set** `V(G)/Aut_S` ‚ÄĒ the vertices of the quotient graph. | `abbrev` |
| `orbitMk` / `orbitMk_eq_iff` | The quotient map `v ‚Ü¶ ‚ü¶v‚üß`; `orbitMk v = orbitMk w ‚ÜĒ OrbitPartition adj P S v w`. | Definition / `Quotient.eq` |
| `cell_iff_orbitMk_eq` | 226-242 | ¬ßA4 **The cell = quotient-vertex lemma.** Under `CellsAreOrbits`, two vertices share a 1-WL cell of `(G, S)` iff they are the same quotient vertex ‚ÄĒ the correspondence B1's cascade-composition induction steps through. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `QuotientAdjCompatible` | 246-254 | ¬ßA4 **Quotient-adjacency compatibility.** The condition that `adj v w` is constant on `Aut_S`-orbit pairs ‚ÄĒ exactly when a simple induced adjacency on the quotient is well-defined (holds at discreteness, fails for coarser `S`). | Definition |
| `quotientAdj` / `quotientAdj_mk` | The induced adjacency on `OrbitQuotient`, well-defined under `QuotientAdjCompatible` (via `Quotient.lift‚āā`); `quotientAdj h ‚ü¶v‚üß ‚ü¶w‚üß = adj.adj v w` (`rfl`). | Definition / `@[simp]` |
| `quotientAdjCompatible_of_discrete` | 269-280 | ¬ßA4 At discreteness the quotient graph is always well-defined (orbits are singletons) ‚ÄĒ the recursion-bottom anchor, paralleling `cellsAreOrbits_of_discrete`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `orbitPartition_empty_iff_orbitRel` | 290-302 | ¬ßA4 The root orbit relation `OrbitPartition adj P ‚ąÖ` equals the `AutGroup` `MulAction` orbit relation (under `P`-invariance) ‚ÄĒ the relational form of the A2 orbit bridge, symmetrised for `orbitRel`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `orbitQuotientEquivAutGroup` | 304-312 | ¬ßA4 **The root quotient is `V(G)/Aut(G)`.** Under `P`-invariance, `OrbitQuotient adj P ‚ąÖ` is equivalent to the `MulAction` orbit quotient of `AutGroup adj`, tying A4's relational quotient back to A1/A2's group object. | Definition |

| `stabilizer_eq_bot_of_isPretransitive_comm` | 324-342 | **(seal core L1, [exhaustive-obstruction ¬ß0.7](../docs/chain-descent-exhaustive-obstruction.md))** A transitive, faithful, **abelian** action is **free**: every point-stabilizer is trivial ("transitive abelian ‚üĻ regular"). The textbook root of "no non-consumed abelian species". | ‚ÄĒ |
| `existsUnique_smul_of_isPretransitive_comm` | 344-355 | **(seal core L2)** Unique candidate: in a transitive faithful abelian action exactly one group element moves `a` to `b` (existence from transitivity, uniqueness from L1's trivial stabilizer). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `smul_eq_on_orbit_of_comm` | 357-366 | **(seal core L3 ‚ÄĒ load-bearing, axiom-free)** Quotient-free, faithfulness-free form: if `g, h` both move `a` to `b` then they agree on the **whole orbit** of `a` (`g‚ÄĘc = k‚ÄĘb = h‚ÄĘc` for `c = k‚ÄĘa`). The "unique-candidate-on-the-cell" the linear-oracle harvest reads ‚ÄĒ holds for an abelian residual even with non-trivial global stabilizers (CFI). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `aut_agree_on_orbit_of_comm` | 368-382 | **(seal instantiation)** L3 for `AutGroup adj`: an **abelian residual** ‚üĻ two automorphisms both sending `a ‚Ü¶ b` agree on every `c` in `a`'s orbit, so the decision is determined on its cell (always consumable). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `not_comm_of_orbit_disagree` | 384-393 | **(seal headline ‚ÄĒ no non-consumed abelian species)** Contrapositive: a decision `a ‚Ü¶ b` whose two candidate automorphisms **disagree** on the cell forces a **non-abelian** residual. With the ¬ß12 capstone (large primitive non-abelian ‚üĻ Cameron), the only non-consumed symmetry is a Cameron section ‚ÄĒ the bottom-up, citation-free half of the seal. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `card_eq_of_isPretransitive_comm` | 404-418 | **(seal Step 4 ‚ÄĒ order side, [exhaustive-obstruction ¬ß0.7](../docs/chain-descent-exhaustive-obstruction.md))** A transitive, faithful, **abelian** action has `Nat.card G = Nat.card őĪ`: the orbit map `g ‚Ü¶ g‚ÄĘa` is a bijection (free from L1, surjective from transitivity), so order = degree ("abelian primitive ‚üĻ regular, hence small"). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `not_comm_of_isPretransitive_of_stabilizer_ne_bot` | 420-426 | **(seal Step 4, qualitative)** A transitive faithful action with a **non-trivial** point stabilizer (not regular) is **non-abelian** ‚ÄĒ direct contrapositive of L1. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `not_comm_of_isPreprimitive_card_lt` | 428-437 | **(seal Step 4 ‚ÄĒ the headline: large primitive ‚üĻ non-abelian)** A **preprimitive** faithful action with `Nat.card őĪ < Nat.card G` (group strictly larger than its degree) is **non-abelian**, since a transitive abelian action has order = degree. The order-side proof that a primitive abelian group is `Z_p` (never large); closes the bottom-up route's Step 4 with no citation. | ‚ÄĒ |
## ChainDescent/Cascade.lean

> **‚ėÖ SEAL CAPSTONE MAP** (also at the top of the seal section in `Cascade.lean`). 22 public
> `reachesRigidOrCameron_*` capstones remain here (12 superseded ones were archived to
> `PrivateTheoremIndex.md`). **The one to use: `reachesRigidOrCameron_viaBoundedMinMult`**
> (`CascadeAffine.lean`; seal `modulo {G3 + hSmallAutThin + hcatch + hImprim}`, open content =
> `hSmallAutThin` = node 4). Other LIVE endpoints: `‚Ä¶_viaNoCover` (poly node-4 anchor),
> `‚Ä¶_viaSmallAutShatters` (sub-exp citation), `‚Ä¶_viaSpielman` (**the fully-citable Cameron-free sub-exp FLOOR
> ‚ÄĒ carries only `hSpielman`, no G3/Cameron/hImprim**), `‚Ä¶_viaG0powNeg` (closure discharged), `‚Ä¶_affineSlice`
> (cited 2-sep), `‚Ä¶_viaCompleteBase` / `‚Ä¶_viaRainbowRank` (node-2 rung). Everything else here is a load-bearing
> intermediate of the live proof chain; the 12 superseded capstones now live (full text) in `PrivateTheoremIndex.md`.

B1 (Tier 3a cascade composition) of `docs/chain-descent-tier3-tractable-buildout.md`,
Phases A + C. Build plan: `docs/chain-descent-tier3a-b1-build-plan.md`. The headline
"depths add" theorem, **conditional on the per-layer transfer** (`LayerStep`, = paper
¬ß4.2.5, discharged in the not-yet-built Phase D). Stays on `Fin n` (no quotient
re-typing) by telescoping cumulative individualization sets. Axiom-clean (standard
basis; `refineStep` via `warmRefine`).

### Phase A ‚ÄĒ interface

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `IsBase adj P T` | **Phase A interface.** `T` is a *base* of the `P`-preserving automorphism group: its pointwise stabilizer is trivial, so the `Aut_T`-orbit relation is equality ‚ÄĒ the chain's bottom `H_k = {1}`. | Definition |
| `LayerStep adj P T S` | **Phase A interface ‚ÄĒ the per-layer transfer obligation.** `CellsAreOrbits T ‚Üí CellsAreOrbits (T ‚ą™ S)`: individualizing the increment `S` brings cells down to `Aut_{T‚ą™S}`-orbits (paper ¬ß4.2.5 transferred to `G`). The contract the composition induction consumes; discharged in Phase D. | Definition |
| (cascade-class predicate) | `RecoverableByDepth adj P bound` (in `CascadeOracle.lean`) ‚ÄĒ Tier-1 (`recoverableByDepth_cfi`) / Tier-2 (`recoverableByDepth_scheme`) instances already proved. | (existing) |

### Phase C ‚ÄĒ composition theorem

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `discrete_of_cellsAreOrbits_base` | 83-90 | **(C1) Finish.** At a base `T` where cells already coincide with `Aut_T`-orbits, warm refinement at `T` is `Discrete` ‚ÄĒ the cascade reaching full canonization. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cellsAreOrbits_compose` | 92-105 | **(C2) Composition induction.** From layer 1's unconditional `CellsAreOrbits` at `T 0` and a `LayerStep` at each subsequent layer, `CellsAreOrbits` holds at the final cumulative set `T k`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cumulative_card_le` | 107-113 | **Depths add (cardinality).** The cumulative individualization set `‚čÉ_{i‚Č§k} S i` has size at most `ő£_{i‚Č§k} f i` when each layer is bounded by its depth `f i`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cascadeComposition` | 115-127 | **Theorem 3a (cascade composition) ‚ÄĒ headline, conditional form.** Cumulative sets with layer-1 recoverability, per-layer transfer steps, and the final set a base ‚üĻ warm refinement at `T k` reaches the discrete partition; with `cumulative_card_le` the cascade depth is `‚Č§ ő£ fŠĶĘ`. Conditional on the `hstep` obligations (= ¬ß4.2.5, Phase D). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cascadeComposition_single` | 135-138 | **Single-layer sanity check (k = 0).** One cascade-class layer that is a base reaches discreteness ‚ÄĒ recovers the Tier-1/Tier-2 orbit-recovery theorems as the composition's base case. | ‚ÄĒ |

### Phase D ‚ÄĒ discharging `LayerStep` (the ¬ß4.2.5 transfer), intrinsic route

Approach B (build-plan ¬ß3): stay on `Fin n`, reduce `LayerStep` to a witness-upgrade via
**set-monotonicity** of warm refinement (reusing `refineStep_iff`); the materialized-quotient
route was rejected (`refineStep` axiomatic, no cross-size API).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `Refines Ōá‚āĀ Ōá‚āā` | `Ōá‚āĀ` refines `Ōá‚āā`: the partition of `Ōá‚āĀ` is finer (`Ōá‚āĀ a = Ōá‚āĀ b ‚Üí Ōá‚āā a = Ōá‚āā b`). The partition order used for warm-refinement monotonicity. | Definition |
| `signature_refines` | 156-177 | **Crux of warm-refinement monotonicity.** If `Ōá‚āĀ` refines `Ōá‚āā`, equal `Ōá‚āĀ`-signatures give equal `Ōá‚āā`-signatures, since `signature Ōá‚āā` is the coarsening of `signature Ōá‚āĀ`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `iterate_refineStep_refines` / `warmRefine_refines_initial` | warm refinement monotone in the initial colouring's partition order. | axiom-light |
| `individualizedColouring_refines` | 203-215 | Individualizing a superset gives a finer initial colouring: `T ‚äÜ T'` ‚üĻ `individualizedColouring n T'` refines `individualizedColouring n T`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `warmRefine_indiv_mono` | 217-225 | **Set-monotonicity (the payoff).** Same `(T ‚ą™ S)`-cell ‚üĻ same `T`-cell: 1-WL is monotone in the individualization set. The load-bearing lemma the docs had mis-cited as `warmRefine_refines`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `WitnessUpgrade adj P T S` | **The genuine ¬ß4.2.5 content.** For `v, w` in the same `Aut_T`-orbit and the same `(T ‚ą™ S)`-cell, the orbit relation upgrades to `Aut_{T‚ą™S}`. The Phase-D interface predicate. | Definition |
| `layerStep_of_witnessUpgrade` | 239-246 | **The reduction ‚ÄĒ where Phase C meets the per-layer content.** A `WitnessUpgrade` discharges a `LayerStep`, via set-monotonicity then `CellsAreOrbits T` then the upgrade. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `layerStep_empty` / `layerStep_subset` / `layerStep_of_cellsAreOrbits` / `layerStep_of_discrete` | Trivial real instances: no-op layer (`S = ‚ąÖ`), `S ‚äÜ T`, independently-recoverable target, and the discretizing recursion-bottom. | axiom-light |
| `witnessUpgrade_of_pathFixing` | 271-286 | **Bridge to harvested generators.** If every same-orbit, same-cell pair admits a `P`-preserving automorphism whose support avoids `T ‚ą™ S` (fixes the committed path) and sends `v ‚Ü¶ w`, the witness-upgrade holds ‚ÄĒ exactly what the cascade/linear oracles produce. | ‚ÄĒ |

### Step 5 ‚ÄĒ the synthesis (Theorem 3a reduced to harvested generators)

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `cascadeComposition_pathFixing` | 305-326 | **Theorem 3a, reduced to harvested path-fixing generators.** Cumulative sets by increments, layer-1 recoverable, every layer's residual symmetry realized by path-fixing automorphisms (`hwit`), and the final set a base ‚üĻ discrete warm refinement at `T k`. Reduces all of Theorem 3a to the single hypothesis of per-layer path-fixing witness existence. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cascadeComposition_twoLayer` | 328-343 | **Smallest genuine composition.** An outer cascade-class layer at `T‚āÄ`, an inner path-fixing layer with increment `S`, and the union a base ‚üĻ discreteness ‚ÄĒ the `CFI(scheme)` / `Scheme(CFI)` shape. | ‚ÄĒ |

**Phase 6b ‚ÄĒ CFI gadget flips discharge the Tier-3a `hwit`.** The Stage-3 gadget flip (`CFI.lean ¬ß15`)
discharges `cascadeComposition_pathFixing`'s `hwit` for a CFI layering, conditional only on the per-layer
existence of committed-set-avoiding gadget flips (the cascade-1b content).

| Name | Description | Notes |
|------|-------------|-------|
| `CFILayerGadgetFlippable` | Per-layer CFI gadget-flip existence: for each layer and same-orbit/same-cell pair `(v,w)`, an even-symmetric cycle `F` whose flip maps `v ‚Ü¶ w` with `T i ‚ą™ S i` in `F`-free gadgets. The `hwit` analog of the linear oracle's `CFIGadgetFlippableLocal`. | Definition |
| `cfiLayer_pathFixing_hwit` | **The `hwit` drop-in.** `CFILayerGadgetFlippable` (+ `P` Aut-invariant) ‚üĻ the Tier-3a `hwit` hypothesis, directly via `cfiFlipAut_pathFixing_witness`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `cascadeComposition_cfi` | **Theorem 3a for CFI layers.** A CFI layering whose residual orbit maps are realised by committed-set-avoiding gadget flips reaches the discrete partition ‚ÄĒ `cascadeComposition_pathFixing` with `hwit` discharged by the Stage-3 flips (conditional only on the cascade-1b cycle existence). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `recoverableByDepth_of_pathFixing_layers` | 413-431 | **The harvest-window connector.** Lands `cascadeComposition_pathFixing`'s `Discrete` output onto the harvest `RecoverableByDepth` conclusion: a layer chain with per-layer path-fixing `hwit` and a base endpoint gives `RecoverableByDepth adj P b` at the chain-length bound. | ‚ÄĒ |

| `ResidualAut` | 461-467 | **Residual automorphism.** A `P`-preserving automorphism of `adj` fixing `S` pointwise ‚ÄĒ an element of the residual group `Aut_S^P`; the building block of the screen predicates. `OrbitPartition adj P S v w ‚ÜĒ ‚ąÉ ŌÄ, ResidualAut ŌÄ ‚ąß ŌÄ v = w`. | Definition |
| `ResidualAbelian` | 469-474 | **D2 ‚ÄĒ abelian residual.** The residual group `Aut_S^P` is abelian (any two residual automorphisms commute) ‚ÄĒ the screen's hidden-abelian / linear leg (calculator ¬ß6); the `¬¨IsBase`-guarded form is the D2 disjunct. | Definition |
| `orbitPartition_iff_residualAut` | 476-482 | `OrbitPartition adj P S v w` unfolds to a `ResidualAut` carrying `v ‚Ü¶ w`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `ResidualInvolutive` | 512-518 | **D2, the exponent-2 form.** Every residual automorphism is an involution ‚ÄĒ `Aut_S^P` has exponent ‚Č§ 2 (an elementary-abelian `Z‚āā^d`, CFI's gauge group). The precise form of D2 the swap content needs; strictly stronger than `ResidualAbelian`. | Definition |
| `residualAbelian_of_involutive` | 520-529 | **Exponent-2 ‚üĻ abelian.** A residual group of involutions commutes ‚ÄĒ wiring the abstract `ResidualAbelian` predicate to the precise `ResidualInvolutive`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `orbitPartition_swap_of_involutive` | 531-544 | **An involutive orbit witness is a swap.** With an exponent-2 residual, an `Aut_S`-orbit pair `a, b` has a residual automorphism with `g a = b` *and* `g b = a` ‚ÄĒ closing the map-vs-swap gap class-agnostically (the content the CFI route obtains from gadget involutions). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `swap_of_cellsAreOrbits_involutive` | 546-556 | **The class-agnostic swap certificate at a recoverable node.** Where orbit recovery holds (`CellsAreOrbits`) and the residual is exponent-2, every same-cell decision pair carries a swapping orbit automorphism ‚ÄĒ the linear oracle's 'a swap exists' input from recovery + D2, replacing the per-class `CFIGadgetFlippable` derivation. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `residualAut_eq_one_of_isBase` | 558-565 | Under a base (`IsBase`), every residual automorphism is the identity ‚ÄĒ it can move no point. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `residualAbelian_of_isBase` | 567-572 | **Trichotomy base case.** A trivial residual (under `IsBase`) is vacuously abelian, so `ResidualAbelian` holds at any base. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `residualAbelian_mono` | 574-581 | **D2 inherited down the descent.** `ResidualAbelian` passes from `S` to any `S' ‚äá S` (the residual shrinks to a subgroup of an abelian group). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `StabilizerAt` | 593-616 | **Part A (A1) ‚ÄĒ the residual group `Aut_S^P` as a `Subgroup`.** Carrier the `P`-preserving automorphisms fixing `S` pointwise (`ResidualAut`); closure via `ResidualAut.mul`. The group object underlying the stabilizer chain. | Definition |
| `mem_stabilizerAt` | 618-619 | Membership: `ŌÄ ‚ąą StabilizerAt adj P S ‚ÜĒ ResidualAut adj P S ŌÄ` (`Iff.rfl`). | `@[simp]` |

| `covered_sound` | 715-723 | **(A2) Covered ‚üĻ sound prune (capstone).** A candidate in the orbit (under verified path-fixing harvested gens) of an explored rep is genuinely `Aut_S^P`-equivalent to it ‚ÄĒ `CoveredByPathFixingAut` soundness. | ‚ÄĒ |

| `card_stabilizerAt_eq_orbit_mul` | 777-786 | **(A3) The order recursion.** `|Aut_S^P| = |orbit of b| ¬∑ |Aut_{insert b S}^P|` ‚ÄĒ the inductive step of `order = ‚ąŹ basic-orbit sizes`, via `Subgroup.card_mul_index` + `index_stabilizer`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `orbitSizeProd` | 797-803 | **(A3.5)** The basic-orbit-size product along an ordered base sequence `bs` from `S`: each `b` contributes `|orbit b under Aut_S^P|`, then the residual descends to `Aut_{insert b S}^P`. | `card_stabilizerAt_eq_prod` | 805-817 | **(A3.5) The telescoping order identity.** For any sequence `bs`, `|Aut_S^P| = orbitSizeProd bs S ¬∑ |Aut_(accumulated)^P|` ‚ÄĒ induction on `bs` over `card_stabilizerAt_eq_orbit_mul`; no computable BSGS. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `card_stabilizerAt_eq_prod_of_base` | 819-826 | **(A3.5) `order = ‚ąŹ basic-orbit sizes` at a base.** When `bs.foldl ‚Ä¶ S` is a base the trailing residual is trivial, so `|Aut_S^P|` is exactly the orbit-size product ‚ÄĒ the abstract `Order = ‚ąŹ OrbitSize` of `PermutationGroup.cs`, no computable BSGS. | ‚ÄĒ |

| `exists_greedy_base_aux` | 847-902 | **(A3.6 ‚ÄĒ greedy-base existence, strong-induction core; step 2.1)** For every bound `N` on `|Aut_S^P|`, a base sequence `bs` from `S` with `2 ^ bs.length ‚Č§ |Aut_S^P|`. Greedy: while `¬¨IsBase`, a residual aut moves a point `b` whose basic orbit is `‚Č• 2`, so inserting `b` strictly shrinks the residual order (`card_stabilizerAt_eq_orbit_mul`) and each layer doubles the lower bound. | `exists_greedy_base` | 904-911 | **(A3.6 ‚ÄĒ `2 ^ |base| ‚Č§ |Aut(G)^P|`)** The `S = ‚ąÖ` headline of `exists_greedy_base_aux`: a base sequence from `‚ąÖ` whose length is logarithmic in the residual order. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `exists_greedy_base_le_log` | 913-921 | **(A3.6 ‚ÄĒ `base(G) ‚Č§ log‚āā|Aut(G)^P|`, the conservation budget's base term banked; step 2.1)** The greedy base length is `‚Č§ Nat.log 2 |Aut(G)^P|`; for a small (poly-order) residual this is `O(log n)`, so the seal's `bound` is `O(log n) + s(C)` with only the `s(C)` stickiness left open. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `gensAt` | 943-948 | **(A2-complete) Path-fixing generators at `S`.** The subset `{g ‚ąą gens | g ‚ąą StabilizerAt adj P S}` ‚ÄĒ generators fixing the committed path. | `gensAt_anti` | 950-954 | **(A2-complete)** Path-fixing generators shrink as the path grows: `S ‚äÜ S' ‚Üí gensAt ‚Ä¶ S' ‚äÜ gensAt ‚Ä¶ S` (via `stabilizerAt_mono`). | ‚ÄĒ |

| `card_closure_gensAt_eq_prod_of_coversOrbits` | 1103-1111 | **(A2-complete) Capstone ‚ÄĒ the chain reproduces the residual order.** With A3.5, coverage gives `Nat.card (Subgroup.closure (gensAt adj P gens S)) = orbitSizeProd adj P bs S` (= `‚ąŹ basic-orbit sizes`): the folded path-fixing generators recover both the residual group and its order. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `residualInvolutive_mono` | 1135-1141 | **(A2-complete, de-classed) `ResidualInvolutive` inherited down the descent.** `ResidualInvolutive S ‚Üí S ‚äÜ S' ‚Üí ResidualInvolutive S'` ‚ÄĒ a subgroup of an exponent-2 group has exponent ‚Č§ 2; the involutive analogue of `residualAbelian_mono`, letting the de-classed coverage carry its hypothesis down the base sequence. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `coversOrbits_of_realizers` | 1143-1168 | **(A2-complete, de-classed ‚ÄĒ general/non-abelian) `CoversOrbits` from per-level path-fixing realizers.** If at every level `T ‚äá S` the harvested `gens` contains a residual-at-`T` realizer for each orbit-mate of each base point (`g ‚ąą gens ‚ąß ResidualAut adj P T g ‚ąß g b = w`), and `bs` ends at a base, then `CoversOrbits adj P gens bs S`. **No group-structure hypothesis** ‚ÄĒ abelian *or* non-abelian (schemes, Cameron) ‚ÄĒ the honest "covers everything, no class ladder" coverage core; `coversOrbits_of_residualInvolutive` is its exponent-2 corollary. | ‚ÄĒ |

| `coversOrbits_of_visibleRealizers` | 1210-1227 | **(A2-complete, de-classed ‚ÄĒ harvest-facing) `CoversOrbits` from realizers keyed on the refinement-visible cell relation.** Same as `coversOrbits_of_realizers` but the realizer hypothesis ranges over same-`warmRefine`-cell pairs (polynomially computable) rather than `OrbitPartition` pairs (orbits refine cells, so it covers a fortiori). | `closure_eq_stabilizerAt_of_realizers` | 1229-1241 | **(A2-complete, de-classed ‚ÄĒ general) Harvest completeness from realizers.** `Subgroup.closure (gensAt adj P gens S) = StabilizerAt adj P S` from per-level path-fixing realizers (`coversOrbits_of_realizers` + `stabilizerAt_eq_closure_gensAt_of_coversOrbits`). | `orbitRealizers_iff_visibleRealizers_of_cellsAreOrbits` | 1243-1261 | **(A2-complete, localisation core) Recovery makes the harvest refinement-decidable.** At a node `T` with `CellsAreOrbits`, the refinement-visible realizer hypothesis (same-`warmRefine`-cell pairs, computable) is *equivalent* to the orbit realizer hypothesis (`OrbitPartition` pairs). `‚Üí` free (`subset_warmRefine`), `‚Üź` uses recovery. Pins localisation as the **polynomiality layer**: coverage correctness holds from orbit realizers unconditionally (`coversOrbits_of_realizers`); recovery makes the equivalent target refinement-computable. Per-level recovery down the base sequence is the substrate-conditional remainder. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `closure_eq_stabilizerAt_of_visibleRealizers` | 1263-1278 | **(A2-complete, polynomiality capstone ‚ÄĒ group side, computable interface)** `Subgroup.closure (gensAt adj P gens S) = StabilizerAt adj P S` from per-level path-fixing realizers keyed on **same-`warmRefine`-cell** pairs (refinement-computable), not `OrbitPartition` pairs. The honest harvest interface: `coversOrbits_of_visibleRealizers` + the A2-complete equality. Visible-realizer hypothesis satisfiable exactly on the recoverable class (`orbitRealizers_iff_visibleRealizers_of_cellsAreOrbits`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `crossBranchHarvest_reproduces_residual` | 1280-1300 | **(A2-complete, the general polynomiality capstone)** From per-level path-fixing **visible** (cell) realizers + a terminal base, **both** `closure (gensAt adj P gens S) = StabilizerAt adj P S` **and** the order `Nat.card ‚Ä¶ = orbitSizeProd adj P bs S` (= `‚ąŹ basic-orbit sizes`). ## ChainDescent/CoherentConfig.lean

The **general (multi-fiber) coherent-configuration substrate** ‚ÄĒ Stage 0/1 of the general-CC
separability build (`docs/chain-descent-general-cc-separability.md`; Stage-0 decision + increment log
in its ¬ß8). Lands the `CoherentConfig` type (colour-function presentation, fibers *derived*), the
homogeneous coercion, the general-CC `AlgIso`/`Separable` (the ¬ßS.17 widening the Stage-1.3 soundness
gate demanded), the probe-validated Thm 4.1 hypothesis predicates (`Theorem41ConditionsProbe.cs`),
the cited `Theorem41Statement` (the staging-fallback carry), and the point extension as a universal
property ‚ÄĒ **plus its ¬ßCC.8 construction (Stage 1.2, 2026-06-12)**: the coherent closure
`pointExtension X T` via a pair-refinement saturation (setoid `pairStep`, representative-indexed
counts, `n¬≤`-round pigeonhole), discharging `IsPointExtension` constructively
(`isPointExtension_pointExtension` / `exists_isPointExtension` / `isPointExtension_unique`).
Axiom-clean `[propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound]`, no `sorry`.

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `CoherentConfig` | 48-74 | **The general (multi-fiber) coherent configuration** on `Fin n`, by its colour function `relOf : Fin n ‚Üí Fin n ‚Üí Fin rank` + four axioms (classes nonempty, transpose well-defined, reflexive classes purely diagonal, intersection numbers constant). The central missing object the live build creates; the point extension `X_T` (non-homogeneous) is why it exists. | Structure |

| `CoherentConfig.le_of_numClasses_le` | 473-485 | **The rigidity half of the pigeonhole**: a refinement with no more classes is no refinement ‚ÄĒ `s' ‚Č§ s` with `numClasses s' ‚Č§ numClasses s` forces `s ‚Č§ s'` (a surjection between equal-card finite quotients is injective). | `CoherentConfig.stableSetoid_pairCount` | 545-552 | **The fixpoint property, extracted**: same stable class ‚üĻ *all* intersection counts agree ‚ÄĒ this IS the coherence axiom of the closure, read off the fixed point. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.pairCount_swap` | 556-575 | Counts of the swapped pair under a swap-stable partition are a pure reindexing: `pairCount s v u x y = pairCount s u v y.swap x.swap` ‚ÄĒ the combinatorial core of the closure's transpose axiom. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.pairIter_swap` | 577-596 | **Every stage is swap-stable** (the transpose invariant): the initial partition respects `Prod.swap` (`X.transpose_eq` + flag swap), and `pairCount_swap` carries it through each round ‚ÄĒ yields the closure's `transpose_eq`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.pairCount_eq_of_zrel` | 600-716 | **The counting heart of the universal property.** A coherent fission `Z` whose classes refine the pair partition `s` has `s`-counts constant on `Z`-classes: decompose fiberwise over `Z`'s class pairs (`card_eq_sum_card_fiberwise`), the `s`-conditions are constant on each fiber (transport along `hle`), and `Z.inter_card_eq` equates the fibers. The ¬ßCC.2 fiber-coherence argument generalized, exactly as the build doc's Stage-1.2 plan predicted. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.zrel_le_pairIter` | 718-748 | **A coherent fission of `X` with `T`-singleton fibers refines every stage of the chain** ‚ÄĒ base case from `Refines Z X` + derived fiber coherence (`relOf_diag_left_eq` reads the flags off `Z`'s classes via the singleton hypothesis); inductive step = `pairCount_eq_of_zrel`. | `CoherentConfig.boundedConfusionMultiplicity_univ` | 2532-2546 | ¬ßCC.22b (non-vacuity anchor, route ¬ß9.6) **The cascade hypothesis is satisfiable ‚ÄĒ the every-graph fallback at `M=n`.** `BoundedConfusionMultiplicity B n` holds for every CC: `S=univ` completes the extension (`c(X_univ)=0`), so `2¬∑0 ‚Č§ c(X_T)`. The route's content is `M=O(log n)`; this exhibits an honest inhabitant guarding the **vacuity trap** (cf. `SchemeReproduced`), mirroring `cascadesAt_univ`/`recoverableByDepth_univ`. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.boundedConfusionMultiplicity_of_completeBase` | 2548-2568 | ¬ßCC.22e (node-2 rung bridge) **A bounded *discrete* base ‚üĻ bounded confusion multiplicity.** If a base `T‚āÄ` (`|T‚āÄ|‚Č§M`) discretizes `X` (the őī‚Ä≤ engine's output), then `BoundedConfusionMultiplicity B M` for every `B` (taking `S:=T‚āÄ` halves `c(X_T)` outright). Sharpens the trivial `boundedConfusionMultiplicity_univ` (`M=n`) to `M=|T‚āÄ|` ‚ÄĒ the bridge from a őī‚Ä≤ bounded base to the `‚Ä¶viaBoundedMultiplicity` pipeline. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.confusionSet_perm` | 2580-2597 | ¬ßCC.22c (route ¬ß9.9 step D1) **Confusion sets are equivariant under a CC automorphism.** For a `relOf`-preserving permutation `ŌÄ` (the `Refines.aut_descends` convention), `C(ŌÄ őĪ, ŌÄ ő≤) = ŌÄ '' C(őĪ,ő≤)`. The structural core of "a persistent big-confusion cover is a rigid `Aut`-invariant line system" (D1) ‚ÄĒ the object the D2 extraction / D3 dichotomy classify. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.card_confusionSet_perm` | 2599-2605 | ¬ßCC.22c (D1) **Confusion size is a CC-automorphism invariant.** `|C(ŌÄ őĪ, ŌÄ ő≤)| = |C(őĪ,ő≤)|` (`confusionSet_perm` + injectivity). So `c(X)` and the "big" (`>c/2`) threshold are `Aut`-invariant ‚ÄĒ the load-bearing D1 fact: big-ness travels with the automorphism group. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.mem_confusionSet_perm` | 2607-2616 | ¬ßCC.22c (D1) **Incidence equivariance.** `ŌÄ v ‚ąą C(ŌÄ őĪ, ŌÄ ő≤) ‚ÜĒ v ‚ąą C(őĪ,ő≤)` ‚ÄĒ the (vertex, confusion-set) incidence is `Aut`-equivariant, so `ŌÄ` carries a cover to a cover and preserves each vertex's multiplicity profile. The atom the cover-rigidity / `minMult`-invariance arguments consume. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.big_confusion_perm` | 2618-2625 | ¬ßCC.22c (D1) **"Big" is a CC-automorphism invariant.** `(őĪ,ő≤)` has an over-half confusion set iff its `ŌÄ`-image does (`card_confusionSet_perm`), so `ŌÄ` permutes the big confusion pairs among themselves ‚ÄĒ the big-class line system is `Aut`-stable, as the D2/D3 classification requires. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.confusionMultiplicity` | 2627-2634 | ¬ßCC.22c (D1, route ¬ß9.6) **The confusion multiplicity (cover-load) of a vertex** ‚ÄĒ the number of big confusion *pairs* `(őĪ,ő≤)` (`őĪ‚Č†ő≤`, `c(X)<2¬∑|C(őĪ,ő≤)|`) that `v` fails to distinguish (`v‚ąąC(őĪ,ő≤)`). The ¬ß9.6 load quantity; its `min` over `v` is `minMult` (the cleanup cost of one halving). Pair form (`‚Č•` the distinct-set `bigClasses` count); bounding it bounds the cleanup `M`. | Definition, `noncomputable` |
| `CoherentConfig.confusionMultiplicity_perm` | 2636-2675 | ¬ßCC.22c (D1, the multiplicity punchline) **Confusion multiplicity is a CC-automorphism invariant.** `confusionMultiplicity (ŌÄ v) = confusionMultiplicity v` for a `relOf`-preserving `ŌÄ`: the product map `(őĪ,ő≤)‚Ü¶(ŌÄőĪ,ŌÄő≤)` bijects the big pairs `v` lies in onto those `ŌÄv` lies in (`big_confusion_perm`+`mem_confusionSet_perm`+injectivity). So cover-load is **constant on automorphism orbits** ‚ÄĒ `minMult` is `Aut`-invariant, and on a vertex-transitive scheme it is literally constant `= L = (ő£_{big}|C|)/n` (no min-vs-average slack). The D1 deliverable: the cover's load profile is rigid. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.BoundedMinMult` | 2685-2690 | ¬ßCC.22d (route ¬ß9.6/¬ß9.9) **Bounded minimum multiplicity** ‚ÄĒ at every over-`B` base, some vertex lies in `‚Č§ M` big confusion pairs (`confusionMultiplicity ‚Č§ M`), i.e. `minMult ‚Č§ M`. The sharpest *computable* form of the ¬ß9.6 cover-load hypothesis (the probe's `minMult`); the thin side of the ¬ß9.9 dichotomy. Carried, never an `axiom`. | Definition |
| `CoherentConfig.boundedConfusionLoad_of_boundedMinMult` | 2692-2722 | ¬ßCC.22d (route ¬ß9.6 ‚ÄĒ **the `(1+L)`-cleanup, formalized**) **Bounded `minMult` ‚üĻ bounded confusion load.** A least-loaded `v` (in `‚Č§ M` big pairs) builds the hitting set `S = {v} ‚ą™ {őĪ : (őĪ,ő≤) big through v}`, `|S|‚Č§M+1`, distinguishing every big pair: `v` kills the big pairs it avoids, and for a big pair through `v` the endpoint `őĪ‚ąąS` distinguishes it (`relOf őĪ őĪ ‚Č† relOf őĪ ő≤`). `BoundedMinMult B M ‚üĻ BoundedConfusionLoad B (M+1)`. The ¬ß9.6 cleanup made rigorous. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `CoherentConfig.boundedConfusionMultiplicity_of_boundedMinMult` | 2724-2732 | ¬ßCC.22d **Bounded `minMult` ‚üĻ the cascade-rate hypothesis** ‚ÄĒ `BoundedMinMult B M ‚üĻ BoundedConfusionMultiplicity B (M+1)` (cleanup ‚ąė load-bridge). Reduces the entire cascade open content to **"the residue has bounded `minMult`"** (the probe quantity); feeds `reachesRigidOrCameron_viaBoundedMultiplicity` ‚Üí the polynomial seal. Axiom-clean. | ‚ÄĒ |

## ChainDescent/GaussCount.lean

The finite-field quadratic exponential-sum toolkit for Stage B.1c-ii (the "Gauss build"): the Mathlib-absent
affine-quadric point count and its multi-point / k-fold generalizations. Imports ONLY Mathlib (a cheap leaf in
`namespace ChainDescent`); ported from the former `ScratchGauss.lean` development file. The endpoint it feeds is
`IsotropySeparatesAtBase` in `CascadeAffine.lean`, discharged via the planned `FormsGraph`-side consumer that
imports both this module and `CascadeAffine`. All decls axiom-clean `[propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound]`.

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `count_eq_charsum` | 40-52 | **Brick A** ‚ÄĒ the solution count `#{x | f x = c}` as a double character sum `‚ąĎ‚āď‚ąĎ‚āú Ōą(t(f x‚ąíc))` (additive orthogonality). The entry point for all the point counts. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_sq` | 54-82 | **Brick B1** ‚ÄĒ the 1-D quadratic Gauss sum `‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(x¬≤) = gaussSum Ōá Ōą` (each `y` hit by `Ōá(y)+1` roots; the `+1` part vanishes). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_smul_sq` | 84-106 | **Brick B2** ‚ÄĒ the scaled 1-D sum `‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(a¬∑x¬≤) = Ōá(a)¬∑gaussSum Ōá Ōą` for a unit `a` (via `gaussSum_mulShift`, `Ōá(a)¬≤=1`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `addChar_sum` | 108-114 | **Helper** ‚ÄĒ an additive character turns a finite sum into a product: `Ōą(‚ąĎŠĶĘ aŠĶĘ) = ‚ąŹŠĶĘ Ōą(aŠĶĘ)`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_quadForm` | 116-148 | **Brick B3** ‚ÄĒ the multivariable quadratic Gauss sum `‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(Q x) = (‚ąŹŠĶĘ Ōá(wŠĶĘ))¬∑gaussSum^d` for nondegenerate `Q` (diagonalize via `equivalent_weightedSumSquares`, factor). The multivariable core. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_quadForm_eval` | 150-186 | **Brick B3‚Ä≤** ‚ÄĒ basis-explicit `sum_addChar_quadForm` (weights `Q(v i)` for an orthogonal basis `v`; value pinned, no existential). Powers the scaling relation. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_quadForm_smul` | 188-225 | **Brick C-scale** ‚ÄĒ scaling the form by a unit `s` scales the Gauss sum by `Ōá(s)^d`: `‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(s¬∑Q x) = Ōá(s)^d¬∑‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(Q x)` (change of additive character). For `d` even, scale-invariant. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_quadForm_smul_ne_zero` | 227-250 | **(M2 ‚ÄĒ the cancellable constant)** If `‚ąĎ_x Ōą(Q x) ‚Č† 0` then `‚ąĎ_x Ōą(s¬∑Q x) ‚Č† 0` for any unit `s` (factor `Ōá(s)^d` is a unit). This is the global Gauss value that cancels when comparing two configurations' multi-point sums `S(r) = Ōą(Gram-expr)¬∑‚ąĎ_x Ōą(R¬∑Q x)`, yielding `Ōą(Gram-expr_u) = Ōą(Gram-expr_{u'})`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `gaussSum_sq_ne_zero` | 252-268 | ‚ÄĒ | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_quadForm_ne_zero` | 270-287 | ‚ÄĒ | ‚ÄĒ |
| `card_quadForm_eq` | 289-328 | **Brick C ‚ÄĒ THE affine-quadric point count (Mathlib-absent).** `#{x:Q x=c}¬∑q = #V + (‚ąĎ_{t‚Č†0} Ōą(‚ąítc)¬∑Ōá(t)^d)¬∑‚ąĎ‚āď Ōą(Q x)`, from Brick A + the scaling relation. The assembled count formula. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_quadForm_linear` | 330-358 | **Brick D1 ‚ÄĒ complete the square.** `‚ąĎ_w Ōą(r¬∑Q w + polar Q w a') = Ōą(‚ąír‚ĀĽ¬Ļ¬∑Q a')¬∑‚ąĎ_w Ōą(r¬∑Q w)` (linear term absorbed by the shift `w ‚Ü¶ w + r‚ĀĽ¬Ļa'`). The engine of hyperplane-section / joint counts. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `count2_eq_charsum` | 360-380 | **Brick A2** ‚ÄĒ the two-condition count `#{x:f x=c ‚ąß g x=d}` as a double-indexed character sum (generalizes Brick A). The entry point for the k-fold count assembly (the Gauss endpoint). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `quad_sub` | 382-390 | **Helper** ‚ÄĒ the parallelogram identity `Q(a‚ąíb) = Q a + Q b ‚ąí polar Q a b`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `polar_sum_right` | 392-400 | **Helper** ‚ÄĒ `polar Q z ¬∑` is additive over a finite sum in its second argument: `‚ąĎ‚Īľ r‚Īľ¬∑polar Q z t‚Īľ = polar Q z (‚ąĎ‚Īľ r‚Īľ‚ÄĘt‚Īľ)` (via `polarBilin`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_multiQuad` | 402-440 | **Multi-point quadratic Gauss sum (generalizes D1) ‚ÄĒ THE inner sum of the k-fold count.** `‚ąĎ_z Ōą(‚ąĎ‚Īľ r‚Īľ¬∑Q(z‚ąít‚Īľ)) = Ōą(const)¬∑‚ąĎ_z Ōą(R¬∑Q z)` for `R=‚ąĎr‚Īľ‚Č†0` (summand collapses to D1 via `quad_sub`+`polar_sum_right`). The engine for the count at a symmetry-broken base. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `countk_eq_charsum` | 442-472 | **Brick A_k ‚ÄĒ the k-fold count as a product-of-sums.** Generalizes `count_eq_charsum`/`count2_eq_charsum` to a `Fintype`-indexed family of conditions: `‚ąĎ_x ‚ąŹ_j (‚ąĎ_{r_j} Ōą(r_j(f_j x‚ąíc_j))) = #{x:‚ąÄj, f_j x=c_j}¬∑q^{#őĻ}` (product of orthogonality indicators). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `countk_eq_sum_charsum` | 474-504 | **Brick A_k factored ‚ÄĒ the k-fold count over dual variables.** `#{x:‚ąÄj, f_j x=c_j}¬∑q^{#őĻ} = ‚ąĎ_{r:őĻ‚ÜíF} Ōą(‚ąí‚ąĎ_j r_j c_j)¬∑‚ąĎ_x Ōą(‚ąĎ_j r_j¬∑f_j x)` (expand via `Fintype.prod_sum`, collapse via `addChar_sum`). With `f_j x = Q(x‚ąít_j)` the inner sum is exactly `sum_addChar_multiQuad` ‚ÄĒ the closed-form multi-point `Q`-count for the symmetry-broken-base injectivity (the Gauss endpoint). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_linearMap` | 505-541 | **The linear-functional character sum (boundary engine).** `‚ąĎ_x Ōą(ŌÜ x) = |V|¬∑[ŌÜ=0]` for a `K`-linear functional `ŌÜ` and primitive `Ōą` (translation by `x‚āÄ` with `Ōą(ŌÜ x‚āÄ)‚Č†1`, from primitivity). Evaluates the `R=‚ąĎr_j=0` boundary of the multi-point count. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `sum_addChar_multiQuad_zero` | 543-570 | **Multi-point quadratic Gauss sum, the `R=0` boundary** (companion to `sum_addChar_multiQuad`). When `‚ąĎ_j r_j=0` the `R¬∑Qz` term vanishes and the summand is linear: `‚ąĎ_z Ōą(‚ąĎ_j r_j¬∑Q(z‚ąít_j)) = Ōą(‚ąĎ_j r_j¬∑Q t_j)¬∑‚ąĎ_z Ōą(polar Q z (‚ąí‚ąĎ_j r_j‚ÄĘt_j))`; the surviving factor evaluates by `sum_addChar_linearMap`. Together with `multiQuad` (R‚Č†0), evaluates the inner sum for ALL `r`. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `count_pi_setValued` | 572-596 | **The inclusion‚Äďexclusion engine ‚ÄĒ value-SET counts = sum of value-POINT counts.** `#{z : ‚ąÄj, h_j z ‚ąą A_j} = ‚ąĎ_{c‚ąą‚ąŹA_j} #{z : ‚ąÄj, h_j z = c_j}` (fiberwise partition additivity). With `h_j z = Q(z‚ąít_j)` it turns isotropy-class counts (each class = a `Q`-value-set: anisotropic ‚ÜĒ `K‚ąĖ{0}`, isotropic-or-zero ‚ÜĒ `{0}`) into the pointwise `Q`-value counts the Gauss toolkit closes. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `multiCharSum_eq_sum_count` | 598-624 | **(M2 hinge ‚ÄĒ Fourier inversion)** `‚ąĎ_x Ōą(‚ąĎ_j r_j¬∑f_j x) = ‚ąĎ_{c:őĻ‚ÜíF} Ōą(‚ąĎ_j r_j¬∑c_j)¬∑#{x:‚ąÄj, f_j x=c_j}` (partition `x` by value-tuple). The dual of `countk_eq_sum_charsum`: all pointwise counts agree ‚üĻ all multi-point Gauss sums `S(r)` agree. With `f_j x=Q(x‚ąít_j)`, `S(r)` carries the Gram (`sum_addChar_multiQuad`), so count-agreement ‚üĻ Gram-agreement. Elementary (no primitivity/domain). | ‚ÄĒ |
## ChainDescent/FormsGraphConcrete.lean

The `FormsGraph`-side consumer (imports `CascadeAffine` + `GaussCount`) that discharges `IsotropySeparatesAtBase Q T`
for the rank-3 SRG `VO^őĶ` residue, combining the Gauss point-count toolkit with the affine substrate + isotropy
dictionary. Build order: (1) count transport `Fin(p^d) ‚ÜĒ V`; (2) isotropy‚Üívalue-set conversion; (3) injectivity.

| Name | Line | Description | Notes |
|------|------|-------------|-------|
| `count_transport` | 26-45 | **Count transport `Fin(p^d) ‚ÜĒ V` along `affineE`.** A vertex count over the affine point set whose predicate factors through `affineE.symm` equals the count over `V = Fin d ‚Üí ZMod p`. Moves the `IsotropySeparatesAtBase` counts into the vector space where the Gauss point counts live. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `qvalue_count_transport` | 46-60 | **`Q`-value-set count on the affine point set ‚Üí pointwise `Q`-counts in `V` (step 2, value-set part).** Chains `count_transport` (`Fin(p^d)‚ÜíV`) with `count_pi_setValued` (set‚Üípoint): `#{z : ‚ąÄj, Q(zŐĄ‚ąít_j)‚ąąA_j} = ‚ąĎ_{c‚ąą‚ąŹA_j} #{x : ‚ąÄj, Q(x‚ąít_j)=c_j}` ‚ÄĒ landing on the pointwise counts the Gauss toolkit closes. The isotropy conditions reduce to such `Q`-value-sets via `isoClass_eq_*` (modulo the origin correction). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `isotropy_count_transport` | 70-94 | **(M1 step 1)** The fine `IsotropySeparatesAtBase` count over `Fin(p^d)` equals the count over `V` (`z‚Č†u ‚ÜĒ affineE.symm z ‚Č† affineE.symm u` + `count_transport`) ‚ÄĒ transports the hypothesis into `V` where the conversion + Gauss closed form live. | ‚ÄĒ |
| `isoSetOf` | 96-99 | The isotropy-class value-set for a coarse bit: anisotropic (`true`) ‚Ü¶ `{2}`, isotropic-or-zero (`false`) ‚Ü¶ `{0,1}`. | Definition |
| `qSetOf` | 101-104 | The matching `Q`-value-set: anisotropic ‚Ü¶ `{x‚Č†0}`, isotropic-or-zero ‚Ü¶ `{0}`. | Definition |
| `mem_isoSetOf_iff` | 106-116 | **(M1 dictionary)** `isoClass Q w ‚ąą isoSetOf b ‚ÜĒ Q w ‚ąą qSetOf b` ‚ÄĒ the coarse split is a pure `Q`-value condition (from `isoClass_ne_two_iff` / `isoClass_eq_two_iff`). | ‚ÄĒ |
| `coarse_eq_sum_iso` | 117-134 | **(M1 core ‚ÄĒ fine‚Üícoarse)** A coarse `Q`-value-set count `#{x:‚ąÄj, Q(x‚ąít_j)‚ąąqSetOf(ŌĄ_j)}` = the sum over refining isotropy profiles `ŌÉ‚ąą‚ąŹisoSetOf(ŌĄ_j)` of fine counts `#{x:‚ąÄj, isoClass(x‚ąít_j)=ŌÉ_j}` (`count_pi_setValued` at the isotropy value-type). So fine-count agreement ‚üĻ coarse-count agreement, no origin correction (M0). | ‚ÄĒ |
